Trump and [Elon Musk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk "Elon Musk")'s [Department of Government Efficiency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_of_Government_Efficiency "Department of Government Efficiency") largely dismantled several federal agencies including [USAID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USAID "USAID") and the [Department of Education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education "United States Department of Education"), unilaterally fired several thousand staff, and reduced administrative functions to statutory minimums.[[525]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-530)[[526]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-531)[[527]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-532) Some actions, such as attempts to dismantle the [Consumer Financial Protection Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consumer_Financial_Protection_Bureau "Consumer Financial Protection Bureau"), were paused by federal courts.[[528]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-533) Many of his actions attempted to bring historically independent institutions under direct executive branch control in diminished forms.[[529]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-534)

### Targeting political opponents

Main article: [Targeting of political opponents and civil society under the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Targeting_of_political_opponents_and_civil_society_under_the_second_Trump_administration "Targeting of political opponents and civil society under the second Trump administration")

During his second presidency, the Trump administration took a series of actions using the government to target political opponents and [civil society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_society "Civil society"). His actions were described by the media as part of his promised "retribution" and "revenge" campaign, within the context of a strongly personalist and leader-centered conception of politics.[[530]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-535)[[512]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Collinson-517)[[531]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-536) He threatened, signed executive actions, and ordered investigations into his political opponents, critics, and organizations aligned with the Democratic Party.[[532]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-537) He ended the post-[Watergate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watergate_scandal "Watergate scandal") norm of [Justice Department](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice "United States Department of Justice") independence, weaponizing it and agencies across the federal government to target his political enemies.[[533]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-538)[[534]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-539) He continued filing personal lawsuits against his political opponents, companies, and news organizations that angered him.[[535]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-540) By July 2025, Trump had extracted more than $1.2 billion in settlements in a "cultural crackdown" against a variety of institutions that largely chose to settle rather than fight back.[[536]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-541)[[537]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-542) Trump's actions against civil society were described by hundreds of legal experts and political scientists as [authoritarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian "Authoritarian"), contributing to [democratic backsliding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_backsliding_in_the_United_States "Democratic backsliding in the United States"), and negatively impacting the [rule of law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_law "Rule of law").[[538]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-543)[[539]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-544)[[540]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-545)

### Pardons and commutations, 2025â€“present

Further information: [List of people granted executive clemency in the second Trump presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_people_granted_executive_clemency_in_the_second_Trump_presidency "List of people granted executive clemency in the second Trump presidency")

Trump's pardons and grants of clemency favored political allies and loyalists,[[541]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-546)[[542]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Thrush_May292025-547) and disproportionately pardoned "the powerful, famous, well-connected and wealthy" accused of white-collar crime.[[542]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Thrush_May292025-547) Trump [granted clemency to all January 6 rioters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pardon_of_January_6_United_States_Capitol_attack_defendants "Pardon of January 6 United States Capitol attack defendants") convicted or charged on his first day in office, including those who violently attacked police, by pardoning more than 1,500 and commuting the sentences of 14.[[543]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Reilly2025-548)[[544]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-NPR2025-549)

### Domestic policy, 2025â€“present

Main articles: [Domestic policy of the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestic_policy_of_the_second_Trump_administration "Domestic policy of the second Trump administration"), [Economic policy of the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_policy_of_the_second_Trump_administration "Economic policy of the second Trump administration"), [Education policy of the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_policy_of_the_second_Trump_administration "Education policy of the second Trump administration"), [Science policy of the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_policy_of_the_second_Trump_administration "Science policy of the second Trump administration"), and [Persecution of transgender people under the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_transgender_people_under_the_second_Trump_administration "Persecution of transgender people under the second Trump administration")

Trump inherited a resilient economy from the Biden administration, with increasing economic growth, low unemployment, and declining inflation.[[545]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-550) He ordered agencies to stop enforcement of disfavored rules in an attempt at large-scale deregulation that legal experts described as illegal and contrary to decades of federal law.[[546]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-551)[[547]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-552) He sought greater government control over private businesses and shifted away from traditional conservative [free market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_market "Free market") orthodoxy,[[548]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-553) engaging in [state capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_capitalism "State capitalism") by taking direct government equity stakes in multiple U.S. corporations.[[549]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-554)[[550]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Economist_08132025-555)[[551]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-556)

Trump [canceled and paused federal grants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_United_States_federal_government_grant_pause "2025 United States federal government grant pause") and made large cuts to scientific research,[[552]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-557) several of which were found by judges and the [Government Accountability Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_Accountability_Office "Government Accountability Office") as being illegal and unconstitutional.[[553]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-558)[[554]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-559) Trump and his administration's [Make America Healthy Again](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Make_America_Healthy_Again "Make America Healthy Again") agenda promoted [anti-science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-science "Anti-science") and [anti-vaccine activism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-vaccine_activism "Anti-vaccine activism"), resulting in a resurgence of whooping cough and measles.[[555]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-560)[[556]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-561)

He promoted [climate change denial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_denial "Climate change denial") and misinformation,[[557]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-562) appointed oil, gas, and chemical lobbyists to the [United States Environmental Protection Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency "United States Environmental Protection Agency") (EPA) to reverse climate regulations and pollution controls,[[558]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-563) and by October 2025 had cancelled $7.6 billion in funding for clean energy projects approved by the previous administration.[[559]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-564)

Trump relied on declaring national emergencies to justify hundreds of actions and bypass congressional approval or regulatory review.[[560]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-565) For instance, he declared a national energy emergency, allowing the suspension of environmental regulations, loosening the rules for fossil fuel extraction and limiting renewable energy projects.[[561]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-566)[[562]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-567) Trump withdrew the U.S. from the [Paris Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Agreement "Paris Agreement") on climate change during his first presidency, [Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Joe_Biden "Presidency of Joe Biden") reentered the agreement in 2021, and Trump again withdrew from the agreement during his second presidency.[[563]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-568)

Dismantling government agencies enforcing the laws against political corruption and white-collar fraud,[[564]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-569) Trump reduced the Department of Justice's [Public Integrity Section](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_Integrity_Section "Public Integrity Section") from 30 to five lawyers,[[565]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-570)[[566]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-defang-571) dismissed 17 independent [inspectors general](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inspector_general#United_States "Inspector general") at government agencies[[567]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-572) and 12 members of independent oversight boards and watchdog agencies,[[568]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-573) and disbanded the squad in the FBI's Washington field office that investigated allegations of fraud and corruption against government officials and members of Congress.[[569]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-squad-574)[[570]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-575) He pardoned or dropped charges against officials accused of corruption.[[569]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-squad-574)

Trump attributed societal problems to [diversity, equity, and inclusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diversity,_equity,_and_inclusion "Diversity, equity, and inclusion") (DEI) initiatives and [wokeness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woke#United_States "Woke").[[571]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Green250203-576) Equating diversity with incompetence,[[571]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Green250203-576) he reversed pro-diversity policies in the federal government.[[572]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-577)[[573]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-578) He sought to remake civil society to his preferences by executive order.[[574]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-579)[[575]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-APfirms-580) On DEI and antisemitism grounds, he threatened cultural institutions[[576]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-581) and sixty universities,[[577]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-WSJed-582) and forced law firms to capitulate to his political agenda.[[575]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-APfirms-580)

Trump expanded the domestic use of the military and ordered [military deployments to several Democratic Party-led cities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_deployment_of_federal_forces_in_the_United_States "2025 deployment of federal forces in the United States"), and threatened to expand his deployments further.[[578]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-583)[[579]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-584) Trump had crews [demolish the White House's East Wing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Wing#Demolition "East Wing") in October 2025 to make room for a [White House State Ballroom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_State_Ballroom "White House State Ballroom"), which is planned to be nearly twice the size of the White House.[[580]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-585)[[581]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-586)

Through [a series of executive orders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_transgender_people_under_the_second_Trump_administration#Executive_Orders "Persecution of transgender people under the second Trump administration") and other actions, Trump banned trans people from the military,[[582]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-587) restricted or defunded gender-affirming healthcare, opposed [inclusive language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inclusive_language "Inclusive language"),[[583]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-588) censored research and education materials,[[584]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-589) and targeted schools, universities, and cultural institutions accused of promoting what his government calls "gender ideology",[[585]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-npr-ideology-590) barred transgender athletes from sports, and required US passports to state transgender people's sex assigned at birth.[[586]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-591)

#### One Big Beautiful Bill Act

In July 2025, Trump signed the [One Big Beautiful Bill Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One_Big_Beautiful_Bill_Act "One Big Beautiful Bill Act") into law. The bill made the temporary tax cuts of the 2017 [Tax Cuts and Jobs Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_Cuts_and_Jobs_Act "Tax Cuts and Jobs Act") permanent and added additional tax deductions for a total of around $4.5 trillion, mostly benefiting the highest income brackets and costing people in the lowest income bracket $1,600 per year. It increased funding for national defense, deportations, the border wall, and Trump's proposed [Golden Dome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Dome_(missile_defense_system) "Golden Dome (missile defense system)") missile defense system. It removed tax credits for renewable energy sources such as wind and solar power and for buyers of electric vehicles. The bill cut funding for [Medicaid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicaid "Medicaid") and [SNAP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supplemental_Nutrition_Assistance_Program "Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program") and added additional work requirements for eligibility and a $35 co-payment for some Medicaid services; the cuts and additional requirements will take effect after the 2026 general election. The bill was projected by the [Congressional Budget Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_Budget_Office "Congressional Budget Office") to increase the budget deficit by $3.4 trillion by 2034, cause 11.8 million people to lose Medicaid coverage, and eliminate SNAP benefits for three million people.[[587]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-592)[[588]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-593)

### Immigration, 2025â€“present

Main articles: [Immigration policy of the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_policy_of_the_second_Trump_administration "Immigration policy of the second Trump administration") and [Deportation in the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deportation_in_the_second_Trump_administration "Deportation in the second Trump administration")

Further information: [Mexicoâ€“United States border crisis Â§Second Trump administration (2025â€“present)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border_crisis#Second_Trump_administration_(2025%E2%80%93present) "Mexicoâ€“United States border crisis"), and [Mexicoâ€“United States border wall Â§Second Trump administration (2025â€“present)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border_wall#Second_Trump_administration_(2025%E2%80%93present) "Mexicoâ€“United States border wall")

In his first days in office, Trump instructed Border Patrol agents to summarily deport [illegal immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States "Illegal immigration to the United States") crossing the border and disabled the [CBP One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CBP_One "CBP One") app that was being used to schedule border crossings. He resumed the [remain in Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remain_in_Mexico "Remain in Mexico") policy, designated drug cartels as terrorist groups, and ordered construction to be resumed on a border wall.[[589]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-594)[[590]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Cbsjan28-595) Trump also revoked the parole status of immigrants who entered the U.S. under CBP One and ended [humanitarian parole for Cubans, Haitians, Nicaraguans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parole_for_Cubans,_Haitians,_Nicaraguans,_and_Venezuelans "Parole for Cubans, Haitians, Nicaraguans, and Venezuelans").[[590]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Cbsjan28-595) In March, he used the [Alien Enemies Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alien_Enemies_Act "Alien Enemies Act") of 1798 to [imprison illegal immigrants without trial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_2025_American_deportations_of_Venezuelans "March 2025 American deportations of Venezuelans") at the [Terrorism Confinement Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorism_Confinement_Center "Terrorism Confinement Center") in El Salvador.[[591]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-596)[Trump targeted activists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Activist_deportations_in_the_second_Trump_presidency "Activist deportations in the second Trump presidency"), legal immigrants, tourists, and students with visas who expressed criticism of his policies or pro-Palestinian advocacy.[[592]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-597) Several [American citizens were detained and deported](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detention_and_deportation_of_American_citizens_in_the_second_Trump_administration "Detention and deportation of American citizens in the second Trump administration").[[593]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-598)

### Foreign policy, 2025â€“present

Main article: [Foreign policy of the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_second_Trump_administration "Foreign policy of the second Trump administration")

Further information: [Tariffs in the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tariffs_in_the_second_Trump_administration "Tariffs in the second Trump administration"), [Chinaâ€“United States trade war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_trade_war "Chinaâ€“United States trade war"), [2025 United States trade war with Canada and Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_United_States_trade_war_with_Canada_and_Mexico "2025 United States trade war with Canada and Mexico"), and [American expansionism under Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_expansionism_under_Donald_Trump "American expansionism under Donald Trump")

His administration favored [hard power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hard_power "Hard power") to achieve its [America First](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/America_First "America First") foreign policy goals,[[594]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-599) and dismantled or withdrew support from domestic and international organizations dedicated to advancing American [soft power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soft_power "Soft power").[[595]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-600)[[596]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-601) The moves were described as ceding American global influence and creating a void filled by [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia") and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China").[[597]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-602)[[f]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-604) Trump's relations with allies were transactional and ranged from indifference to hostility, including threats of annexation.[[599]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-605)[[600]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-606)

Meeting with Zelenskyy, February 2025

In February 2025, Trump and Vice President Vance [berated Ukrainian president Volodymyr Zelenskyy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_Trump%E2%80%93Zelenskyy_Oval_Office_meeting "2025 Trumpâ€“Zelenskyy Oval Office meeting") in a highly contentious televised meeting. Media outlets described it as an unprecedented public confrontation between an American president and a foreign [head of state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state "Head of state").[[601]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Liptak_20250228-607)[[602]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-608)

Trump and his incoming administration helped broker [a Gaza war ceasefire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_2025_Gaza_war_ceasefire "January 2025 Gaza war ceasefire") alongside the Biden administration, enacted a day prior to his inauguration.[[603]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-609)[[604]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-610)[[605]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-credit-611) In March, [Israel broke the ceasefire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_2025_Israeli_attacks_on_the_Gaza_Strip "March 2025 Israeli attacks on the Gaza Strip").[[605]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-credit-611) On October 9, 2025, Israel and Hamas signed an agreement to cease fire and exchange Israeli hostages for Palestinian prisoners as part of the [first phase of Trump's initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_peace_plan "Gaza peace plan") to end the [Gaza war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war "Gaza war").[[606]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-612)

Trump's economic policies have been described as [protectionist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protectionism_in_the_United_States "Protectionism in the United States"),[[607]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-613) with Trump imposing tariffs on most countries, including large tariffs on major trading partners China, Canada, and Mexico.[[608]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-614) He started a global [trade war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_war "Trade war"), imposing tariffs at the highest level since the 1930 [Smootâ€“Hawley Tariff Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smoot%E2%80%93Hawley_Tariff_Act "Smootâ€“Hawley Tariff Act") at the onset of the [Great Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression "Great Depression").[[609]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-615)[[610]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-616) Economists argued that the administration misunderstood the relationship between [trade deficits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balance_of_trade "Balance of trade") and tariffs, using flawed assumptions.[[611]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-617) Trump suspended American financial contributions to the [World Trade Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Organization "World Trade Organization").[[612]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-618)

### Personnel, 2025â€“present

Main articles: [Political appointments of the second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_appointments_of_the_second_Trump_administration "Political appointments of the second Trump administration") and [Second cabinet of Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_cabinet_of_Donald_Trump "Second cabinet of Donald Trump")

In his second term, Trump selected [cabinet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_cabinet_of_Donald_Trump "Second cabinet of Donald Trump") members with personal loyalty to him,[[613]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-619)[[614]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-focus-620) with the "focus on loyalty over subject-matter expertise".[[614]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-focus-620) In February 2025, the White House stated that [Elon Musk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk "Elon Musk") was a [special government employee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_government_employee "Special government employee").[[615]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-musk-621) Trump gave Musk's [Department of Government Efficiency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_of_Government_Efficiency "Department of Government Efficiency") (DOGE) access to many federal government agencies.[[615]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-musk-621) Musk's teams operated in eighteen departments and agencies in the administration's first month,[[616]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-622) including in the Treasury Department's $5 trillion payment system,[[617]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-623) the [Small Business Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Business_Administration "Small Business Administration"), the [Office of Personnel Management](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_Personnel_Management "Office of Personnel Management"), and the [General Services Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Services_Administration "General Services Administration").[[618]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-624)

Beginning with his 2016 campaign, Trump's politics and rhetoric led to the creation of a [political movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_movement "Political movement") known as Trumpism.[[619]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-625) His political positions are [populist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populist "Populist"),[[620]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss2024298-626)[[621]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrbinati2019-627) more specifically described as [right-wing populist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_populist "Right-wing populist").[[622]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTECampaniConcepci%C3%B3nSolerSav%C3%ADn2022-628)[[623]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-629) He has been described as embracing [far-right extremism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far-right_extremism "Far-right extremism"),[[624]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Baker_07272025-630)[[625]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-631) and he helped bring far-right fringe ideas and organizations into the mainstream.[[626]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-632) Many of his actions and rhetoric have been described as [authoritarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian "Authoritarian") and contributing to [democratic backsliding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_backsliding_in_the_United_States "Democratic backsliding in the United States").[[627]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParkerTowler2019505;_513-633) Trump pushed for an expansion of presidential power under a maximalist interpretation of the [unitary executive theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unitary_executive_theory "Unitary executive theory").[[628]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-634)[[629]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-635) His political base [has been compared](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trumpism#Cult_of_personality "Trumpism") to a [cult of personality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cult_of_personality "Cult of personality").[[g]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Cult-643)

Trump's rhetoric and actions have been accused of creating and exacerbating anger and distrust through the use of an ["us" versus "them" narrative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In-group_and_out-group "In-group and out-group").[[637]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss2024299-644) He explicitly and routinely disparages racial, religious, and ethnic minorities,[[638]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStephens-Dougan2021302-645) and scholars consistently find that racial animus regarding blacks, immigrants, and Muslims are the best predictors of support for Trump.[[639]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerman202176-646) His rhetoric has been described as using [fearmongering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fearmongering "Fearmongering") and [demagogy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demagogy "Demagogy") which [intensified during his 2024 presidential campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump_2024_presidential_campaign#Fearmongering "Donald Trump 2024 presidential campaign").[[640]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-647) He has said that he believes real power comes from fear.[[641]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-648) The [alt-right](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alt-right "Alt-right") movement coalesced around and supported his candidacy, due in part to its [opposition to multiculturalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_to_multiculturalism "Opposition to multiculturalism") and [immigration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_to_immigration "Opposition to immigration").[[642]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-649)[[643]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-650)[[644]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-651) He has a strong [appeal to evangelical Christian voters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trumpism#Christian_Trumpism "Trumpism") and [Christian nationalists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_nationalism#United_States "Christian nationalism"),[[645]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerryWhiteheadGrubbs2021229-652) and his rallies take on the symbols, rhetoric, and agenda of Christian nationalism.[[646]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-653) Trump has also used [anti-communist sentiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communism "Anti-communism") in his rhetoric, regularly calling his opponents "[communists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communism "Communism")" and "[Marxists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism "Marxism")".[[647]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-654)[[648]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-655)

### Racial and gender views

Main articles: [Racial views of Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racial_views_of_Donald_Trump "Racial views of Donald Trump") and [Donald Trump sexual misconduct allegations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump_sexual_misconduct_allegations "Donald Trump sexual misconduct allegations")

Many of Trump's comments and actions have been characterized as racist.[[649]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-656) In a 2018 national poll, about half of respondents said he is racist; a greater proportion believed that he emboldened racists.[[650]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-657) Several studies and surveys found that racist attitudes fueled his political ascent and were more important than economic factors in determining the allegiance of Trump voters.[[651]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-658) Racist and [Islamophobic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamophobic "Islamophobic") attitudes are strong indicators of support for Trump.[[652]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTELajevardiOskooii2018-659) He has been accused of racism for insisting a group of five black and Latino teenagers were guilty of raping a white woman in the 1989 [Central Park jogger case](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Park_jogger_case "Central Park jogger case"), even after they were exonerated in 2002.[[653]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-660)

In 2011, Trump became the leading proponent of the racist ["birther" conspiracy theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_citizenship_conspiracy_theories "Barack Obama citizenship conspiracy theories") that Barack Obama, the first black U.S. president, was not born in the United States.[[654]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-661) He claimed credit for pressuring the government to publish Obama's birth certificate, which he considered fraudulent.[[655]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-662) In September 2016, he acknowledged that Obama was born in the U.S.,[[656]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-663) though he reportedly expressed birther views privately in 2017.[[657]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-664) During the 2024 presidential campaign, he made false attacks against the racial identity of his opponent, Kamala Harris, that were described as reminiscent of the birther conspiracy theory.[[658]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-665) His 2024 campaign made extensive use of [dehumanizing language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dehumanization "Dehumanization") and [racial stereotypes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_stereotype "Ethnic stereotype").[[659]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-666) In 2025, he promoted false claims of [white genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_genocide "White genocide") in South Africa[[660]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-667) and created the [White South African refugee program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_South_African_refugee_program "White South African refugee program").[[661]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-668)

Trump has a history of belittling women when speaking to the media and on social media.[[662]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTERotheCollins2019-669)[[663]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Shear-670) He made lewd comments, disparaged women's physical appearances, and referred to them using derogatory epithets.[[663]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Shear-670) As of 2020, 26 women have publicly [accused him of sexual misconduct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump_sexual_misconduct_allegations "Donald Trump sexual misconduct allegations"), including rape, kissing without consent, groping, looking under women's skirts, and walking in on naked teenage pageant contestants. He has denied the allegations.[[664]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-no26-671) In October 2016, a 2005 "[hot mic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_mic "Hot mic")" recording surfaced in which [he bragged](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump_Access_Hollywood_tape "Donald Trump Access Hollywood tape") about kissing and groping women without their consent, saying that, "when you're a star, they let you do it. You can do anything. ... Grab 'em by the [pussy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pussy#Female_genitalia "Pussy")."[[665]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-672) He characterized the comments as "locker-room talk".[[666]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-673)[[667]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-674) The incident's widespread media exposure led to his first public apology, videotaped during his 2016 presidential campaign.[[668]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-675)

### Link to violence and hate crimes

Further information: [Rhetoric of Donald Trump Â§Violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhetoric_of_Donald_Trump#Violence "Rhetoric of Donald Trump")

Trump has been identified as a key figure in increasing political violence in the U.S., both for and against him.[[669]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-676)[[670]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTENacosShapiroBloch-Elkon2020-677)[[671]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiazzaVan_Doren2022-678) He is described as embracing extremism, [conspiracy theories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_conspiracy_theories_promoted_by_Donald_Trump "List of conspiracy theories promoted by Donald Trump") such as [Q-Anon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Q-Anon "Q-Anon"), and far-right [militia movements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_militia_movement "American militia movement") to a greater extent than any modern American president,[[624]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Baker_07272025-630)[[672]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-679) and engaging in [stochastic terrorism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_terrorism "Stochastic terrorism").[[673]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-680)

Research suggests that Trump's rhetoric is associated with an increased incidence of hate crimes,[[674]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-681)[[675]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-682) and that he has an emboldening effect on expressing prejudicial attitudes due to his normalization of explicit racial rhetoric.[[676]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStephens-Dougan2021306-683) During his 2016 campaign, he urged or praised physical attacks against protesters or reporters.[[677]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-684)[[678]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-685) Numerous defendants investigated or prosecuted for violent acts and hate crimes cited his rhetoric in arguing that they were not culpable or should receive leniency.[[679]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-686)[[680]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-687) A nationwide review by [ABC News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ABC_News_(United_States) "ABC News (United States)") in May 2020 identified at least 54 criminal cases, from August 2015 to April 2020, in which he was invoked in direct connection with violence or threats of violence mostly by white men and primarily against minorities.[[681]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-688) Trump's refusal to condemn the white supremacist [Proud Boys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proud_Boys "Proud Boys") during a 2020 presidential debate[[682]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-689) and his comment, "Proud Boys, stand back and stand by", were said to have led to increased recruitment for the pro-Trump group.[[683]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-690) Counterterrorism researchers described his normalization and [revisionist history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_revisionism "Historical revisionism") of the January 6 Capitol attack, and [grant of clemency to all January 6 rioters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pardon_of_January_6_United_States_Capitol_attack_defendants "Pardon of January 6 United States Capitol attack defendants"), as encouraging future political violence.[[684]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-691)[[685]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-692)

### Conspiracy theories

Main article: [List of conspiracy theories promoted by Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_conspiracy_theories_promoted_by_Donald_Trump "List of conspiracy theories promoted by Donald Trump")

Since before his first presidency, Trump has promoted numerous conspiracy theories, including Obama "birtherism", [climate change denial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_denial "Climate change denial"), and [alleged Ukrainian interference in U.S. elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conspiracy_theories_related_to_the_Trump%E2%80%93Ukraine_scandal "Conspiracy theories related to the Trumpâ€“Ukraine scandal").[[686]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-693)[[687]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Haberman2016-694)[[688]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-695) After the 2020 presidential election, he promoted conspiracy theories for his defeat that were characterized as "[the big lie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_lie_(2020_United_States_presidential_election) "Big lie (2020 United States presidential election)")".[[689]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-696)[[690]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-697)

### False or misleading statements

Main article: [False or misleading statements by Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_or_misleading_statements_by_Donald_Trump "False or misleading statements by Donald Trump")

[![Image 31: Chart depicting false or misleading claims made by Trump](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/2017-_Donald_Trump_veracity_-_composite_graph.png/500px-2017-_Donald_Trump_veracity_-_composite_graph.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2017-_Donald_Trump_veracity_-_composite_graph.png)

[Fact-checkers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fact-checkers "Fact-checkers") from _The Washington Post_,[[691]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-database-698) the _Toronto Star_,[[692]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-699) and CNN[[693]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-700) compiled data on "false or misleading claims" (orange background) and "false claims" (violet foreground).

Trump frequently makes false statements in public remarks,[[694]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-finnegan-701)[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-whoppers-147) to an extent unprecedented in [American politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_politics "American politics").[[694]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-finnegan-701)[[695]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-glasser-702)[[696]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Konnikova-703) His falsehoods are a distinctive part of his political identity[[695]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-glasser-702) and have been described as [firehosing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Firehosing "Firehosing").[[697]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKakutani201894%E2%80%93104-704) His false and misleading statements were documented by [fact-checkers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fact-checker "Fact-checker"), including at _The Washington Post_, which tallied 30,573 false or misleading statements made by him during his first presidency,[[691]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-database-698) increasing in frequency over time.[[698]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-TermUntruth-705)

Some of Trump's falsehoods were inconsequential,[[699]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-706)[[700]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-707) while others had more far-reaching effects, such as his unproven promotion of antimalarial drugs as a treatment for COVID-19,[[701]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-708)[[702]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-709) causing a U.S. shortage of these drugs and [panic-buying](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panic-buying "Panic-buying") in Africa and South Asia.[[703]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-710)[[704]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-711) Other misinformation, such as misattributing a rise in crime in [England and Wales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/England_and_Wales "England and Wales") to the "spread of radical Islamic terror", served his domestic political purposes.[[705]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-712) His attacks on mail-in ballots and other election practices weakened public faith in the integrity of the 2020 presidential election,[[706]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-713)[[707]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-714) while his disinformation about the pandemic delayed and weakened the national response to it.[[708]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-NYT_4_11_20-715)[[709]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-USAT-Disinfo-716)[[710]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-717) He habitually does not apologize for his falsehoods.[[711]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-718) Until 2018, the media rarely referred to his falsehoods as lies, including when he repeated demonstrably false statements.[[712]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-719)[[713]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-DBauder-720)[[714]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-721)

### Social media

Main articles: [Social media use by Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_media_use_by_Donald_Trump "Social media use by Donald Trump") and [Twitter use by Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twitter_use_by_Donald_Trump "Twitter use by Donald Trump")

See also: [Personal and business legal affairs of Donald Trump Â§Lawsuits over social media ban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_and_business_legal_affairs_of_Donald_Trump#Lawsuits_over_social_media_ban "Personal and business legal affairs of Donald Trump")

Trump's social media presence attracted worldwide attention after he joined Twitter in 2009. He posted frequently during his 2016 campaign and as president until [Twitter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twitter "Twitter") banned him after the January 6 attack.[[715]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-722) He often used Twitter to communicate directly with the public and sideline the press;[[716]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-gone-723) in 2017, his press secretary said that his [tweets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tweet_(social_media) "Tweet (social media)") constituted official presidential statements.[[717]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-724) During his 2024 campaign and second presidency he frequently posted AI-generated content of himself as [pop-culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pop-culture "Pop-culture") icons or mocking immigrants.[[718]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-725)[[719]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-726)

After years of criticism for allowing Trump to post misinformation and falsehoods, Twitter began to tag some of his tweets with fact-checks in May 2020.[[720]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-727) In response, he said social media platforms "totally silence" conservatives and he would "strongly regulate, or close them down".[[721]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-728) After the January 6 attack, he was banned from [Facebook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facebook "Facebook"), [Instagram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instagram "Instagram"), Twitter, and other platforms.[[722]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-729) The loss of his social media presence diminished his ability to shape events[[723]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-730)[[724]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-731) and correlated with a dramatic decrease in the volume of misinformation on Twitter.[[725]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-732) In February 2022, he launched social media platform [Truth Social](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truth_Social "Truth Social") where he attracted a fraction of his Twitter following.[[726]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-733)[Elon Musk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk "Elon Musk"), after [acquiring Twitter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acquisition_of_Twitter_by_Elon_Musk "Acquisition of Twitter by Elon Musk"), reinstated his Twitter account in November 2022.[[727]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-734)[[728]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-735) The two-year ban at [Meta Platforms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meta_Platforms "Meta Platforms") lapsed in January 2023, allowing him to return to Facebook and Instagram.[[729]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-736)

### Relationship with the press

Further information: [First presidency of Donald Trump Â§Relationship with the news media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_presidency_of_Donald_Trump#Relationship_with_the_news_media "First presidency of Donald Trump"), [Personal and business legal affairs of Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_and_business_legal_affairs_of_Donald_Trump "Personal and business legal affairs of Donald Trump"), and [Donald Trump's conflict with the media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump%27s_conflict_with_the_media "Donald Trump's conflict with the media")

[![Image 32: Trump, seated at the Resolute Desk in the White House, speaking to a crowd of reporters with boom microphones in front of him and public officials behind him](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/President_Trump%27s_First_100_Days-_45_%2833573172373%29.jpg/250px-President_Trump%27s_First_100_Days-_45_%2833573172373%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:President_Trump%27s_First_100_Days-_45_(33573172373).jpg)

Talking to the press, March 2017

Trump sought media attention throughout his career, maintaining a "love-hate" relationship with the press.[[730]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-737) In the 2016 campaign, he benefited from a record amount of free media coverage,[[731]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Cillizza-160614-738) estimated at $2 billion.[[732]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-739) As a candidate and as president, he frequently accused the press of bias, calling it the "fake news media" and "the [enemy of the people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enemy_of_the_people "Enemy of the people")".[[733]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-740)

The first Trump presidency reduced formal press briefings from about one hundred in 2017 to about half that in 2018 and to two in 2019. They also revoked the press passes of two White House reporters, which were restored by the courts.[[734]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-741) His 2020 presidential campaign sued _The New York Times_, _The Washington Post_, and CNN for defamation in opinion pieces about his stance on Russian election interference. All the suits were dismissed.[[735]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-742)[[736]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Atlantic_Press-743) By 2024, he repeatedly voiced support for [outlawing political dissent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criminalization_of_dissent "Criminalization of dissent") and criticism,[[737]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-744) and said that reporters should be prosecuted for not divulging confidential sources and media companies should possibly lose their broadcast licenses for unfavorable coverage of him.[[738]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-745)

In his second term, Trump's actions against the media were unprecedented in modern American history,[[739]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-746) and historians described them as mirroring actions by authoritarian leaders to censor political opponents and negatively impacting the [freedom of speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech") and [free press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_press "Free press").[[740]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-747)[[741]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-748) The campaign to police speech drew comparisons to [cancel culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cancel_culture "Cancel culture"), government [censorship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Censorship "Censorship"), and [McCarthyism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McCarthyism "McCarthyism").[[742]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-749)[[743]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-750)[[744]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-751) Some were sued and many social media companies,[[745]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-752) broadcasters, and newspapers capitulated to the Trump agenda.[[746]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-753) Trump launched lawsuits and created blacklists against certain media outlets, took over the process run by the [White House Correspondents' Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Correspondents%27_Association "White House Correspondents' Association") to choose what outlets have access to him and made a policy of limited access for all wire services.[[747]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-754)[[748]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-755) The [Federal Communications Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission "Federal Communications Commission") launched investigations into media outlets accused of bias against him.[[749]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-756) As a result of Trump's threats, media executives instructed journalists and their staff to [self-censor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-censor "Self-censor") and reduce criticism of Trump,[[750]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-757) and CBS agreed to create an Ombudsman to monitor its news channels to root out "bias" at CBS News.[[751]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-758)

Personal life
-------------

### Family

Further information: [Trump family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump_family "Trump family")

In 1977, Trump married [Ivana ZelnÃ­ÄkovÃ¡](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivana_Zeln%C3%AD%C4%8Dkov%C3%A1 "Ivana ZelnÃ­ÄkovÃ¡").[[752]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlair2015300-759) They had three children: [Donald Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Jr. "Donald Jr.") (b. 1977), [Ivanka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivanka_Trump "Ivanka Trump") (b. 1981), and [Eric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Trump "Eric Trump") (b. 1984). The couple divorced in 1990, following his affair with model and actress [Marla Maples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marla_Maples "Marla Maples").[[753]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-760) He and Maples married in 1993 and divorced in 1999. They have one daughter, [Tiffany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiffany_Trump "Tiffany Trump") (b. 1993), whom Maples raised in California.[[754]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-761) In 2005, he married Slovenian model [Melania Knauss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melania_Knauss "Melania Knauss").[[755]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKranishFisher2017266-762) They have one son, [Barron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barron_Trump "Barron Trump") (b. 2006).[[756]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-763)

### Relationship with Jeffrey Epstein

Main article: [Relationship of Donald Trump and Jeffrey Epstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relationship_of_Donald_Trump_and_Jeffrey_Epstein "Relationship of Donald Trump and Jeffrey Epstein")

Trump had a 15-year friendship with [Jeffrey Epstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Epstein "Jeffrey Epstein"). Persons who knew them at the time said they frequently hit on and competed for women.[[757]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-764) Media attention and public pressure mounted in 2025, when his administration did not release [files relating to Epstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Epstein_client_list "Jeffrey Epstein client list"), despite Trump's promise to do so during the 2024 campaign.[[758]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-765)

### Health

Main article: [Age and health concerns about Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_and_health_concerns_about_Donald_Trump "Age and health concerns about Donald Trump")

Trump says he has never drunk alcohol, smoked cigarettes, or used drugs,[[759]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-766)[[760]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-767) and that he sleeps about four or five hours a night.[[761]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-768)[[762]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlmondDu2020-769) He has called golfing his "primary form of exercise", but usually does not walk the course.[[763]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-770) Trump considers exercise a waste of energy as he believes the body is "like a battery, with a finite amount of energy", which is depleted by exercise.[[764]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-771)[[765]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'DonnellRutherford1991133-772)

In 2015, his campaign released a letter from his longtime personal physician, [Harold Bornstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harold_Bornstein "Harold Bornstein"), stating that he would "be the healthiest individual ever elected to the presidency".[[766]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-dictation-773) In 2018, Bornstein said Trump had dictated the contents of the letter and that three of Trump's agents had seized his medical records in a February 2017 raid on Bornstein's office.[[766]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-dictation-773)[[767]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-774)

### Religion

Main article: [Donald Trump and religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump_and_religion "Donald Trump and religion")

Trump called himself a [Presbyterian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presbyterian "Presbyterian") and a [Protestant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestant "Protestant") in 2016.[[768]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-775)[[769]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-776) In 2020, he said he was a [nondenominational Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nondenominational_Christian "Nondenominational Christian").[[770]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-777) However, many have questioned the depth of these religious affiliations. A survey during his first presidency (2017â€“2021) showed that 63 percent of Americans did not believe that he was religious, despite professing a Christian affiliation, and that only 44 percent of Americans believed Trump was a Christian.[[771]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-778) Some of Trump's comments on the Bible or Christian practice have led critical observers to suggest that his knowledge of Christianity is superficial or erroneous, and few biographers have described him as deeply or even particularly religious.[[772]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-LATimes17-779)[[773]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-NPR16-780)

In his first term, Trump appointed his personal pastor[[774]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-781) and spiritual advisor,[[775]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-782) millionaire televangelist [Paula White-Cain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paula_White-Cain "Paula White-Cain"), to the White House [Office of Public Liaison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_Public_Liaison "Office of Public Liaison").[[776]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-783) During his second term, he appointed her senior advisor of the newly created [White House Faith Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Faith_Office "White House Faith Office").[[777]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-784)[[778]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-785)

Assessments
-----------

### Public image

Main articles: [Public image of Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_image_of_Donald_Trump "Public image of Donald Trump") and [Donald Trump in popular culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump_in_popular_culture "Donald Trump in popular culture")

See also: [Opinion polling on the first Trump presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opinion_polling_on_the_first_Trump_presidency "Opinion polling on the first Trump presidency") and [Opinion polling on the second Trump presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opinion_polling_on_the_second_Trump_presidency "Opinion polling on the second Trump presidency")

In Trump's first term, from 2017 to 2021, international approval ratings of U.S. leadership dropped from about 22 percent in a [Gallup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallup,_Inc. "Gallup, Inc.") poll[[779]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-786) of 134 countries to just 16 percentâ€”lower than China's [Xi Jinping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xi_Jinping "Xi Jinping") and Russia's [Vladimir Putin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin")â€”in a [Pew Research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pew_Research "Pew Research") poll[[780]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-787) of 13 countries. In 2017, estimation of U.S. leadership declined most among allies.[[781]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-788)

Domestically, in his first term, Trump had chiefly partisan support: 88 percent among Republicans and 7 percent among Democrats.[[782]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Jones-789) In a 2021 Gallup poll, he was the only president never to reach a 50 percent approval rating, and he was the first not to be named most admired in his first year in office.[[783]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-790)

In his second term's first quarter according to Gallup, Trump's approval rating was 45 percentâ€”somewhat better than his first term, and far below the 60 percent average of other presidents. Support remained polarized; he had the approval of 90 percent among Republicans, 37 percent among independents, and 4 percent among Democrats.[[784]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-791) His second term also saw large drops in global public opinion of the United States.[[785]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-Henley_06112025-792)

### Scholarly rankings

Further information: [Historical rankings of presidents of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States "Historical rankings of presidents of the United States")

After Trump's first term, [historians ranked Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States#2021_C-SPAN "Historical rankings of presidents of the United States") as the fourth-worst president in [C-SPAN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-SPAN "C-SPAN")'s 2021 survey of presidential historians.[[786]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-793) He rated lowest in the leadership characteristics categories for moral authority and administrative skills.[[787]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-794)[[788]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-795) The [Siena College Research Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siena_College_Research_Institute "Siena College Research Institute")'s 2022 survey [ranked him](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States#2022_Siena_College "Historical rankings of presidents of the United States") third-worst. He was ranked near the bottom in all categories except for luck, willingness to take risks, and party leadership, and ranked last in several categories.[[789]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-scri_22-796) In 2018 and 2024, members of the [American Political Science Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Political_Science_Association "American Political Science Association") ranked him the worst president.[[790]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-797)[[791]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump#cite_note-798)
